Important Domestic News

Central and National Government's Memorial Week 74

At 9:00 AM on the morning of the 3rd, the Central Party Headquarters held the 84th Memorial Week. Members of the Central Committee Sun Ke, Shao Lizi, Liu Luyin, Yu Jingtang, and other guests and staff of the headquarters, totaling more than 300 people, attended. Chairman Sun Ke opened the meeting and performed the ceremony as usual. Shao Lizi then gave a political report, saying in brief, "I followed Comrade Chiang to the front and left the capital for five months. Fortunately, the military campaign has ended, and I am very happy to reunite with my comrades. The most important military event of the past week was Yang Hucheng's occupation of Tongguan on the 25th of last month. He occupied Xi'an on the 27th. Tongguan is more than 300 li away from Xi'an by dry road. In general, people feel that since Yang Hucheng has occupied Tongguan, the recovery of Xi'an is definitely not a problem, but it will always take a considerable amount of time to achieve this goal. Although Song Zheyuan was defeated, his remaining troops still had some ability to resist. Moreover, Xi'an has high city walls and deep moats, and its architecture is extremely solid. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, Yang Hucheng defended Xi'an for eight months. The difficult-to-attack situation of Xi'an can be imagined. As for this time, the two famous cities were captured only three days apart from the capture of Tongguan. The momentum was like a broken bamboo. The difference between the difficulty and ease of the before and after is so great. There must be a reason for this. What is the reason? It is having doctrine versus not having doctrine. From this, we can know that the success of having doctrine and the failure of not having doctrine are even more obvious. However, although the Central Government has won the victory in this great war, it not only dares not be complacent or conceited, but also thinks about danger and fear even more. Why? In China's thousands of years of history, the records of successes and failures are unknown. Those who can permanently maintain their war achievements are actually very few. Moreover, it is common in history for those who become proud of their victory to fail shortly after. Therefore, the Central Government thought about danger and fear and decided before the war to fight for the survival of doctrine, not for personal gains and losses. After the victory in the war, when the doctrine had been consolidated, it first advocated peace in order to seek revolutionary construction. Furthermore, in terms of this great war, after five months, the Central Government's military strength and financial resources were more abundant than those of the enemy, and its equipment was more sophisticated. Moreover, with Commander-in-Chief Chiang's divine strategy and bravery, he was confident in military affairs, and it was impossible not to go through such a long period of time and sacrifice more than 100,000 people. The danger was not just once before victory could be achieved. There is a constant saying among the ancients of China that 'war is fierce and battles are dangerous,' which is not an empty saying. Therefore, those who experience a war must increase their education once. There is a constant saying in the West that civilized countries must increase their progress once after a war. However, looking back at our country's past history, each war only increases one loss. The ancient civilized metropolises and historical sites are destroyed by war, and the people leave their homes because of war. They are innumerable. After the war, thousands of years have passed, and no progress has been made. The reason for this is that they are content with the status quo and do not seek progress. This time, the result of the war is victory for doctrine. From now on, the government and society should all be united in awareness and strive for progress, changing the previous habit of complacency. There must be extreme progress in construction in order to maintain this lasting peace. In terms of military construction, in the past, swords and spears were used. Even if there were guns and cannons, they were all earthen medicine. Today, they are no longer suitable for warfare. Earthen music can only be used to make firecrackers. Although China can manufacture them, foreigners research and improve them every day. The guns and bullets made in China are still not catching up with others. If aircraft can also be manufactured in China, but without gasoline, they cannot fly. Now, China's gasoline must be purchased from foreign countries. If foreigners suddenly stop selling gasoline to China, not only will aircraft not be able to fly, but all kinds of cars will also have to stop. This is a very dangerous thing. We should think about not relying on people and quickly seeking independence. In China's past history, wars arose one after another like a revolving lantern because there was no so-called doctrine, so society was not concerned at all. The people's mentality has not changed until now. After the end of this war, people still say, 'It has been hard work for several months. Now we can take a rest,' as if war is commonplace and future wars are still brewing. This kind of mentality is the most obstructive to peace. Also, after this victory, there are various rumors, saying that a certain institution will be reorganized or that a certain person will be promoted. In fact, these are all speculations, and there is no such thing. This is also caused by old habits and is also a bad mentality. If an official's service is not appropriate, the government has the right to weigh and replace him. If he is diligent in his duties, he will be rewarded for his political achievements and will never be shaken. Just like when I was at the front, I heard rumors in the rear that someone was injured and someone was killed in action. I don't know where these rumors came from, but I can only laugh them off. Now that I have arrived in Beijing, I have heard rumors that someone will be promoted and someone will be transferred. People even ask me about it, but there is nothing to answer, which is really annoying. This kind of speculative mentality should be broken from now on, so that people's minds can be stabilized. The most regrettable thing I felt in this war was that the wounded soldiers were not treated well. The care for the wounded soldiers is entirely a matter for the rear and entirely a matter for society. In the Sino-Japanese and Russo-Japanese Wars, the wounded soldiers were all treated by social organizations, who initiated medical treatment and nursing. Not only was medical material provided in full, but the nurses were mostly female students who personally took care of the wounded soldiers, giving them all kinds of spiritual comfort. Therefore, the wounded soldiers were happy to return to the front and were not afraid to die. In this war, the comfort of the wounded soldiers was only provided by the Lizi Society, with few people and many wounded soldiers, and the equipment was not complete. In addition, social organizations were not involved in comforting the wounded soldiers. Therefore, the wounded soldiers all ran away along the way after being cured and sent to the front. This shows that the lack of love among the Chinese people is the greatest weakness. There is also one thing that is enough to hinder peace, that is, the desires of the Chinese people are never satisfied. Shi Yousan is one of them. In the past, Shi commanded 20,000 to 30,000 troops and was often not satisfied. Later, he had 50,000 to 60,000 and was still not satisfied. Recently, he had 70,000 to 80,000 and still intended to not be satisfied. To fulfill his desires, even if there were more than 100,000 troops, he would still be unsatisfied. If you want to fulfill his desires, I am afraid that the country's financial resources and the society's material resources will not be able to catch up. Now Shi has been appointed by the Central Government and has been incorporated by the Central Government. This is not to criticize Shi intentionally. There is no shortage of people whose desires are similar to Shi's. Shi is taken as an example to generalize the rest. In short, China must leave military affairs in order to seek various types of manufacturing, such as how to improve guns and cannons, how to develop industry and commerce. After this war, all forces have become aware of it. After this, it should not happen, but the crisis with foreign countries is also hidden from this, and we must prepare for it before it rains. We must know that after the European War, the countries are nominally maintaining peace, but in secret they are each preparing their armaments. There will definitely be a greater war in the future that will be more fierce than the previous war. We should be aware of this as soon as possible and prepare for prevention." After the report, the meeting adjourned.

At 10:00 AM on the same morning, the National Government held the Premier's Memorial Week. Zhu Peide, Ma Fuxiang, Jiang Menglin, Kong Xiangxi, He Yaoguo, Zhu Luhe, Wei Daoming, Lin Xiang, Zheng Hongnian, Chen Xi, Wang Jiazhen, Li Jinlun, Chen Yu, Qiu Ao, Wu Siyu, Zhou Yawei, and government civil servants and military staff, totaling more than 200 people, attended. After Zhu Peide took the seat and performed the ceremony, Secretary Qian Changzhao gave the following political report: (Shaanxi has been suffering from natural disasters and man-made disasters for years, and the people are not living well. Fortunately, Xi'an has been recovered, and the government has appointed Yang Hucheng as a member of the Shaanxi Provincial Government and chairman. Comrade Yang has worked very hard to suppress the rebels. Now that he has come out to preside over the provincial administration, it is deeply hoped that he will be able to save the people from the depths of misery. Shaanxi is full of bandits, and suppressing bandits is the first priority. It is imperative to restore social order and enable the people to live and work in peace. At the same time, the weather is getting colder, and disaster relief is also urgent. It is impossible to make the Shaanxi Provincial Government cook without rice. The government and the people of the whole country should do their best to help. As for the active aspects, all construction work should also be planned as soon as possible, because the development of the Northwest can start from Shaanxi. The so-called development of human and financial resources must be carefully prepared. This cannot be done in a short period of time, but we must pay attention to it now and carry it out. The bandit communists in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi are still rampant. In the past, the central government was focused on suppressing the rebels, and the bandit communists were able to survive. Now that the military campaign to suppress the rebels has ended, we should launch a large-scale encirclement and suppression to eliminate them once and for all. The central government is prepared and is moving east. In fact, the bandit communists are not only in the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi. In other provinces, they also openly occupy local areas or are lurking and harming them. The government has decided to carry out a large-scale cleanup. The cleanup is definitely not just empty talk, but more than a year has passed since the announcement of the Cleanup Regulations on September 18th, and there has been little achievement in this matter in various places, and there are even fewer detailed reports. In the future, we must take responsibility and implement it effectively. We must understand that if this matter is not done first, all construction in the country cannot be carried out. We hope that we will make special efforts. The Industrial and Commercial Conference was opened on Saturday and Sunday of last week. The scale is very large. In addition to the representatives sent by the central ministries and commissions and various provinces and cities, there are also appointed members and experts. Some of them have rich experience or have advanced knowledge. Gathering together, the ideals and facts will be considered when discussing various issues. There are many items to be discussed this time, and the issues of relieving unemployment, concentrating capital, coordinating labor and capital, and promoting and protecting domestic goods are particularly important at present. The policy should be decided urgently. It is said that there are three or four hundred proposals in total. It is not easy to examine and discuss them in a short period of time. Fortunately, there are many talents, so they can be competent. It is hoped that all the plans decided in the future will be implemented in order. The government will do its best in both negative aspects, such as eliminating bandit communists and abolishing exorbitant taxes, and positive aspects, such as facilitating transportation and promoting and rewarding industry and commerce. We also believe that the industrial and commercial sectors can absolutely cooperate with the government to establish a long-term foundation for the national economy.)

Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce

Proposed Commercial Accounting Year 75

The Hangzhou City Chamber of Commerce, in order to address the year-end accounting issues for businesses, convened a joint meeting this afternoon (the 3rd) of the chairmen and committee members of various trade associations. Attendees included Shao Yan, Wang Xiangquan, Jin Runquan, Yang Chunlai, and 36 others. Xu Xinggong was unanimously elected as chairman. Committee member Xie Hucheng and others presented a proposal regarding the establishment of a commercial accounting year. After detailed discussion by the attendees, it was resolved to submit the original proposal to the authorities, requesting the establishment of a commercial accounting year with the beginning of Spring, Summer Solstice, and Autumn Equinox as the accounting periods. It was also requested that the final accounting period for this year be extended to February 15th of the following year as a transitional measure. The original proposal is recorded as follows:

1. It is understood that the annual final accounting for business bookkeeping should be conducted in accordance with the Gregorian calendar as determined and mandated by the Party and government agencies, which we merchants should strictly adhere to. However, Chinese commerce traditionally views the beginning and end of agricultural production as a cycle. The time when agricultural production begins is when funds are needed, and the time when it is harvested is when funds are repaid. In the past, the harvest of agricultural products and the repayment of funds occurred close to the end of the lunar year. Merchants therefore set the end of the year as the accounting period, which has become a long-standing custom. While the national calendar can be changed at any time and the public can be strictly required to comply, the natural processes of agricultural production, which are related to climate and seasons, cannot be shifted by human decree. The government's published calendars still predict seasonal changes and list them by month, demonstrating its emphasis on agricultural production and adapting to nature. Similarly, the government's establishment of fiscal years for state finances is undoubtedly intended to balance income and expenditure, which is also related to the processes of agricultural production. Otherwise, it could simply use the calendar year for accounting. The Chamber of Commerce, overseeing commercial activity, has received numerous requests from various industries to adjust the year-end accounting method to accommodate their needs. Merchants in other cities are also making similar requests. Given these circumstances, it seems inappropriate to ignore them. A standard method should be discussed and established to avoid a situation of "cutting the feet to fit the shoes" and to achieve a practical solution. However, the opinions expressed by merchants in various places often focus solely on immediate relief and do not address the fundamental issues. For example, proposals to extend the accounting period to the end of January or February 15th of the Gregorian calendar are understandable, but what is suitable for the present may not be applicable in the future, requiring annual changes and lacking permanence. Therefore, such methods cannot be considered appropriate. In our humble opinion, it is urgent to suggest to the authorities that a commercial accounting year be established, similar to the fiscal year used for state finances, to align with natural cycles and facilitate commerce. The start and end dates of this commercial accounting year should be based on the Gregorian calendar and align with the seasonal changes that are most relevant to the start and end of agricultural work. It is proposed that the annual accounting year begin on the day of the Start of Spring (立春) and end on the day before the Start of Spring of the following year. This approach would better balance national policy with agricultural and commercial practices, making it practical, easy to implement, and permanently established. Furthermore, in the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, commercial practice dictates that funds are typically raised in the spring and autumn to finance the purchase of goods, known as "long-term loans." Traditionally, these loans began and ended in the third and ninth months of the lunar calendar (a period of six months). It is suggested that the Start of Summer (立夏) and Start of Winter (立冬) be used as alternative start and end dates (with the first period lasting 179 days and the second lasting 186 days). Moreover, the government currently sets the end of June, end of September, and end of December as quarterly tax collection dates, but in reality, most businesses face significant difficulties and may even use this as an excuse for delays. It is also suggested that these dates be adjusted to the Start of Spring, Summer Solstice, and Autumn Equinox. This would ensure that government policies and practical realities are aligned. Those who are law-abiding would not suffer unexpected losses, while those seeking illicit gains would have no excuse for procrastination. Consistency and permanence would be ensured. As this matter relates to the vital interests of commerce, we dare not remain silent. We propose that this matter be carefully considered and submitted to the Party and government agencies for selection and implementation. We have drafted a proposal and included a comparative table of the corresponding dates in the Gregorian and lunar calendars for the aforementioned seasonal changes over the past ten years for reference. This is submitted for public decision. (Attached table omitted)

The Crisis of Domestic Soy Sauce 76

Foreign soy sauce is aggressively competing, threatening to eliminate domestic production.

The Legislative Yuan is now proposing measures to provide relief.

Soy sauce is originally a unique product of our country, characterized by its fresh taste and rich nutritional value, and is a daily necessity for the common people. The domestic production volume is very large. Recently, Japan has been promoting the improvement of soy sauce, conducting in-depth research into the cultivation of microbes, and has achieved the goals of shortening the brewing time and improving the quality. In addition, the Japanese government has been providing various incentives, reducing its salt prices and exempting its brewing stone tax, which has sharply reduced costs and improved manufacturing. As a result, there has been aggressive foreign development, and large quantities of products have been imported into our country. Soy sauces from England, Portugal, Russia, and France have also been flowing in. Domestic soy sauce, originally a gourmet condiment, has now suffered a sharp decline and is in danger of disappearing. The reasons for this can be attributed to three major factors: high salt prices, obstructed sales channels, and the widespread circulation of foreign soy sauces. Mr. Zhong Lujian, who is familiar with the soy sauce industry, has already issued a warning in an article, which has attracted the attention of the Chinese people. Now, the Legislative Yuan is also proposing measures to provide relief. An excerpt from the proposal is presented below, hoping that the authorities will pay attention to it.

(Soy sauce is one of the many commodities sold throughout the country without regional restrictions. Unfortunately, in the fifth year of the Republic of China, the salt merchants of the five prefectures of Jiangsu Province, in order to force the sale of salt licenses, lobbied the salt affairs authorities to formulate six separate rules for the sale of salt to soy sauce workshops, so as to force the allocation of expensive salt and restrict the competition of soy sauce. Salt for making soy sauce in one place could not be purchased from another place, and soy sauce made here was not allowed to be sold there. However, these rules were limited to the five prefectures of Jiangsu Province. In the twelfth year of the Republic of China, the Liangzhe Salt Transport Commissioner's Office issued an order limiting the sale of soy sauce to only 50 catties, which was intended to enable salt merchants to force the sale of expensive salt. In the eighteenth year, this was reduced to 10 catties. Jiangzhe soy sauce has no free competition. Later, the Yangtze River port patrol agencies misunderstood the Jiangzhe soy sauce workshop salt rules and also detained and punished those who exported and sold soy sauce to various places. The saying is that pulling one hair moves the whole body. As a result, domestic soy sauce cannot be freely sold, and foreign soy sauce is allowed to be sold freely throughout the country. This is a distorted phenomenon in the current promotion of domestic goods movement that is deeply concerning. Free competition is a necessary condition for general commodities, and improving quality is the result of free competition. They promote each other, and the industrial and commercial industries can only have opportunities for promotion and development. Therefore, the decline of domestic soy sauce today is the result of its inability to be sold.)

Salt used for soy sauce production in European and American countries is classified as industrial salt, and taxes are reduced or exempted. The only purpose is to reduce costs and promote its improvement, so as to develop it to the outside world. Even in neighboring Japan, where the salt monopoly bureau has a high tax rate, the soy sauce industry has been affected by both high taxes on salt and heavy tax on brewing stones. After repeated calls from soy sauce merchants across the country and protests from the industrial sector, the soy sauce tax laws were completely abolished in the fifteenth year of Taisho (1926). Since then, the Japanese soy sauce industry has been able to reduce costs and develop overseas, taking the lead in East Asia. The tax rate on salt used in soy sauce workshops in our country is extremely high. For example, in the five prefectures of Jiangsu Province, the matching price for salt used in soy sauce workshops is 11 yuan, 7 jiao, and 5 fen per dan. The high tax areas in Lianghuai are even higher. In addition, there are also tank donation fees and photo fees, which have caused the cost of soy sauce to increase sharply year by year. As a result, new laws and new manufacturing machines that can promote quality and reduce costs cannot be implemented, and we can only sit back and watch the rapid development of the foreign brewing industry. If this continues, domestic soy sauce will gradually disappear.

Domestic soy sauce is not only burdened by heavy taxes and regional restrictions, but also lacks the ability to actively improve manufacturing and cannot freely sell its products. It is in a precarious situation and cannot last forever, let alone develop overseas. As a result, foreign soy sauce has taken advantage of the opportunity to enter and sell throughout the country. According to customs reports, the net import volume of ordinary soy sauce in recent years is estimated at 4,600,2147 customs taels. The net import volume of caviar and other condiments is more than 21 million taels. The huge amount is already alarming (statistics from Minguo 2 to 17). The amount smuggled into the country cannot be estimated, and the import volume increases year by year. It has doubled in the last three years. Japan has the largest number of imports, followed by England and Portugal, and then Russia and France. Comparing the net import volume of ordinary soy sauce in various countries, it can be proved that the flooding of foreign soy sauce into China is a huge amount. The large amount of imports is transported to the mainland from Dalian, Shanghai, Andong, Jiaozhou, Tianjin, Gongbei, Kowloon, and Qiongzhou and sold in batches. Since imported goods are flooding the country, the disappearance of domestic soy sauce is only a matter of time. In order to provide relief, the industrial and commercial and financial authorities should immediately restore its circulation and reduce its tax rate, so as to improve its products, revitalize industry, and protect domestic products and prevent leakage.

Factions within the Jin Army 77

North China Correspondence: The Jin army units of Li Fuying and Wang Jingguo, which retreated west from Shijiazhuang, are now stationed along the Zhengtai Railway line between Huolu and Jingxing, with only a small number of scattered soldiers patrolling and lacking any defensive works. The majority of their troops have retreated into Niangziguan. Zhang Yinwu, Li Fuying, Wang Jingguo, Li Shengda and others are currently in Niangziguan. Yan Xishan has entrusted Zhang Yinwu with full responsibility for the defense of this area. However, in reality, Zhang can only command Feng Pengzhu's unit. The others, such as Li Fuying, who hails from Yan Xishan's hometown of Wutai County and is a core member of the Jinbei faction and Yan's confidant, continues to receive direct orders from the Taiyuan headquarters. Li Shengda, formerly under Fu Zuoyi, is a core member of the Jinnan faction. Wang Jingguo, whose seniority is above Zhang's, are not subject to Zhang's control. Therefore, if hostilities break out in this area, the Jin army may not be able to hold Niangziguan despite its strategic location, as discord among generals is a major cause of military defeat. The previous disastrous defeat of Fu Zuoyi and others in Jinan was due to this. (Currently, Fu Zuoyi remains in seclusion in the Tianjin concession, not daring to return to support). Traditionally, Shanxi generals have been divided into three factions: Jinnan, Jinbei, and Baoding. The Jinnan faction has declined significantly since the annihilation of Fu Zuoyi's entire army. Currently, the Jinbei and Baoding factions are in a state of tacit rivalry. However, the Jinbei faction is largely composed of people from the Wutai area, such as Yang Aiyuan, Yang Chengyuan (Yan's nephews), Du Chunyi, and Li Fuying (Yan's fellow villagers and neighbors), all of whom Yan has promoted as his most trusted. They are always positioned in the rear during battles and given priority when land is acquired (for example, Yang Aiyuan's appointment as Chairman of Chahar and Li Fuying's appointment as Commander of the Pingjin Garrison). They are always treated better than other factions, so the Jinnan and Baoding factions have often been dissatisfied, and their resentment has intensified after this major defeat. Yan's decision to entrust Zhang (Yinwu) with full responsibility for the defense of Niangziguan is intended to appease the Baoding faction and prevent division. At the same time, he appointed Zhao Chengshou as the Border Defense Commander, responsible for the security of the Yanmen area in northern Shanxi, and Guan Fuan as the Military City Garrison Commander, responsible for the security of eastern Shanxi. As for the allocation of troops, the remnants of Sun Chu, Yang Xiaou, Guan Fuan, and others, who retreated from the Longhai Line, are stationed in Hedong, Linfen, and Yuncheng. The units of the Jinbei faction are mostly stationed in Yanmen, Daizhou, and Datong in northern Shanxi, with Zhang Yinwu, Zhao Chengshou, and Guan Fuan sharing responsibility for the north, south, and east. The rumors that Yan has handed over military power to Xu Yongchang and Shang Zhen are not true. (October 28)

Cao Fulin's troops march east.

Qiao Lizhi's division, stationed in the Zhoucun area, will also be under Cao Fulin's command. Cao Fulin himself is scheduled to depart on the evening train today, accompanied by Chief of Staff Wang Shiqi and Chief of the Operations Section Su Erchang, and will establish his headquarters in Jiaozhou. Currently, the most rampant bandits in Jiaodong include Wang Sida's gang in Linqu, Hao Mingzhu's gang south of Fangzi Station, Wang Ziming's gang between Anqiu and Gaomi, and a gang in Pingdu. Each gang consists of 300 to 600 people and engages in arson, murder, kidnapping, and other evils. It is said that after Cao Fulin arrives in Jiaozhou, he will begin suppression operations. In Jinan, only Li Hanzhang's 85th Brigade of the 29th Division of the 14th Army and Lei Taiping's pistol brigade remain to handle defense duties. In addition, Sun Tongxuan, commander of the 22nd Army, is currently overseeing bandit suppression in Wuding, and Rong Guangxing, commander of the 80th Brigade, is suppressing bandits in the Dongchang area. The situation in southern Shandong has been relatively calm recently. (November 1)

The Yanbian Incident Is Becoming Increasingly Serious 79

More than 500 Japanese police officers have invaded.

They carry weapons and roam the streets, causing alarm among merchants and residents.

Harbin Correspondence: After the Longjingcun incident, the provincial government requested the Yanji Garrison Commander Ji Xing to investigate and report the truth. Recently, due to the expansion of the scope of the negotiations, the provincial government, in accordance with the central government's orders, is unable to respond to the Japanese consulate independently. Therefore, it can only remain calm for the time being. However, the Japanese side is becoming increasingly aggressive. Not only have they refused to withdraw the police officers who invaded Yanbian, but they also dispatched more than 30 additional police officers from Huining, Korea, on the 24th of this month to invade the areas of Toutaogou, Helong, Wangqing, and Baicaogou. Large units of armed Japanese police have also arrived in these areas. In total, more than 500 Japanese police officers have invaded Yanbian, not including those originally stationed in various places. The residents are suffering from the disturbance. In Longjingcun, Japanese police officers patrol the streets all night with weapons. After 8:00 PM, the Chinese all close their doors and remain inside. As a result, the streets are almost empty of people except for the Japanese police officers coming and going. In order to avoid conflicts, Ji Xing's troops have withdrawn the sentries from the streets. Therefore, Yanbian has become the world of the Japanese. In addition to the armed police officers spread along the border, the Japanese side has also dispatched many plainclothes police officers to search the countryside, making it impossible for the villagers to live in peace. Starting on the 25th, the Japanese police in Longjing also implemented a system of inspecting the cleanliness of citizens, overstepping their authority and interfering in our internal affairs. Although the Commercial Port Bureau has protested twice, the Japanese have ignored them. (November 28)

Regulations for the Suppression of Inland River Steamships in Jiangsu 80

The amended Interim Regulations for the Suppression of Inland River Steamships in Jiangsu Province by the Department of Construction have been approved by the Provincial Government. The following is a record of them. (Article 1) The purpose of these Regulations is to rectify inland river navigation and ensure the safety of passengers. (Article 2) Steamships that have been registered and licensed by the Ministry of Communications shall, when opening a service, submit the routes listed in the license to the County Magistrate, who shall forward them to the Department of Construction for submission to the Ministry of Communications for approval before they may operate. (Article 3) All ships shall comply with the customs regulations and restrictions, and shall not be overloaded or have excessively old machinery, nor shall they increase their speed excessively, which may endanger them. (Article 4) Each shift should strictly adhere to the original scheduled time, not earlier or later. (Article 5) Each ship is limited to towing three large vessels or no more than four small vessels. (Article 6) Each ship should set aside a spot at every fixed distance along the route to pile up coal ash on the river bank and not throw it into the river. If this is not observed, and it is discovered, the local authorities may report it to the county government, which may impose a fine of more than ten yuan and less than fifty yuan. (Article 7) Passenger fares, tea room fees, liquor charges, and the reception of passengers on each ship should be in accordance with the following provisions: (A) Each ship's ticket office should follow a fixed fare price and should not add extra charges. (B) Tea room staff, sailors, etc. should deduct a portion of the liquor charges within the ticket price for distribution and should not demand a single cent from passengers. (C) When luggage is stored in the cabin, there are usually nameplates and copper coins of three or four coins each, which should be collected by the shipping office on behalf of the passengers and should not be demanded repeatedly. (D) If passengers sit in seats that are not in their class, the tea room staff and sailors can only advise them to make up for the ticket according to the regulations and should not extort money on the pretext of doing so. (E) All passengers who sit in the passenger cabin should be allowed to sit according to their tickets, and the tea room staff should not hoard them for resale. (Article 8) The person in charge of the shipping office should be responsible for handling matters relating to the shipping office, and the person in charge of the ship should be responsible for handling matters relating to the ship. The County Magistrate should supervise and inspect them at any time together with the County Public Security Bureau. If the above situation is found, the County Magistrate should impose a fine of more than fifty yuan and less than one hundred yuan. (Article 9) If a shipping company does not comply with the provisions of these Regulations, the County Government may detail the circumstances and submit them to the Department of Construction for submission to the Ministry of Communications to cancel the right to sail. (Article 10) These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Embezzlement by Stamp Duty Inspectors: Shao You-tang and Hua Yue-ru, inspectors from the Chengxi branch of the Jiangsu Provincial Stamp Duty Bureau, arrived at the Fulong leather shoe and suitcase store at the north end of Shuyuan Lane in the city around 3 p.m. yesterday to inspect for any unpaid stamp duties. The shop owner, Liu Xiyong, handed over all his account books for inspection. Shao and Hua found that four account books had stamps that they deemed illegal. (Note: Each account book should use stamps for two years. The stamps affixed this year are the current stamps, while the stamps affixed last year were those issued after the current situation became public and were previously in general use.) They declared that according to regulations, a fine of 40 to 400 yuan would be imposed. Liu Xiyong argued that there were no violations or unpaid stamps and offered to pay a fine. After some negotiation, Liu agreed to purchase seven yuan worth of stamps. Shao and Hua instructed Liu to send someone to the bureau to collect the stamps, but when the person returned, they only received two yuan worth of stamps. The remaining five yuan had been pocketed by Shao and Hua.

University Student Attempted Suicide and Rescued: Qian Zhexian, 24, the young owner of the Wansheng Pharmacy in Changzhou Yuncun, is a student at Soochow University in Suzhou and comes from a wealthy family. His father passed away early, and his mother is still alive. Qian has suffered from hemorrhoids (also known as anal inflammation) for years and has consulted numerous famous doctors without success. As a result, he dropped out of school last year and became depressed. He recently sought treatment at Baolong Hospital in Shanghai, but it was still ineffective, which further depressed him. He left home a few days ago, wandering around the scenic spots of Hangzhou, and sent a letter home saying that he was stimulated by the environment and would travel all over the country, making it difficult to determine when he would return. Qian's mother was extremely anxious after receiving the letter and immediately asked her relative Xie Nanxie, nephew Qian Jingchun, and friend Shi Xingda to go to Shanghai, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, and other places to look for him. On the 31st of last month, Qian Zhexian arrived in Wuxi from Hangzhou and stayed in Room 55 of the Qitai Inn on Tongyun Road, using the alias Ying Fu. He had already made up his mind to commit suicide. That night, he wrote two wills, one to his family and one to the inn's front desk. Yesterday morning, Qian locked himself in his room and swallowed three bottles of Midingna tranquilizer pills and went to sleep. In the afternoon, the inn's tea server noticed that he had not gotten up and became suspicious. He opened the door and saw Qian lying stiffly on the bed, his face pale. He then saw three empty bottles of tranquilizer pills and two wills on the table, as well as three yuan in cash. Realizing he had taken poison, he immediately reported it to the front desk. At that moment, Xie Nanxie and Shi Xingda happened to be at the Qitai Inn looking for him. They were extremely alarmed and immediately took Qian Zhexian to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. After examination by Dr. Zhu of the hospital, Qian woke up, but he was still unable to speak. However, his life was likely out of danger. In the evening, Shi Xingda took a boat back to report to Qian Zhexian's mother and brother, who came to Wuxi to take care of him.

Expansion of the Liyang County Magistrate Embezzlement Case: Since the Liyang County Magistrate's old embezzlement case was investigated in the provincial court, the situation has gradually expanded, and the details have become increasingly clear. The case involves various figures in the party and government, as well as local old and new bullies, all colluding with each other and acting as accomplices. One evening, three party affairs workers were arrested in Liyang and sent to the provincial court. Due to it being a weekend, personnel were dispatched for strict surveillance. In addition, Zheng Chengyuan admitted during the interrogation that he was confused and negligent in his inspection and requested that the former officials responsible for the malfeasance be arrested and transferred to the judiciary for thorough investigation so that the truth could be revealed.

Fengxian 85

Widow's Regretful Remarriage Leads to Lawsuit: Jin Chen, a widow from the 41st Tu of Langjia Bridge South, lost her husband early and was unwilling to live alone. She had an affair with her farmhand, Lu Acai, which recently deepened. Seeking a permanent arrangement, Lu offered a "tea gift" of 120 yuan as the cost of becoming her "adopted" husband and officially cohabitated with her on the 20th of last month. Unexpectedly, after the fact, the widow was coerced by her clan uncle, Jin Gou, due to a dispute over the management of her family property, and hastily filed a lawsuit with the county, claiming forced marriage. During the interrogation the day before yesterday, Lu first stated the details of their love affair and claimed that the cohabitation was not of his own volition, providing a signed document as proof. He now regretted it, saying that he was deceived by sweet words and felt ashamed and indignant. The widow gave vague and bizarre statements. After the judge presented evidence and questioned them, Lu revealed the past events, and the widow had no choice but to agree. It is reported that the case was not resolved through mediation, so a summons was issued again yesterday for further interrogation.

Yangzhou 86

Bandits Openly Levying Contributions Door-to-Door: In the Luyang Lake area bordering Jiangdu and Gaoyou, bandit activity has been rampant. According to reports, robberies are frequent. Recently, hundreds of bandits have been entrenched in Chenjia Village, Zhenwu Temple, which belongs to the county. In addition to rifles and Mauser pistols, they are equipped with mortars and hand-held water-cooled machine guns. Yesterday, it was reported that the bandits openly summoned the local township heads, demanding that they raise 20,000 yuan within twelve hours or face the consequences. The bandits sent armed men to accompany the township heads to each household to demand money. If the residents were unable to pay, the bandits initially set fire to their haystacks as a warning, then doused quilts in kerosene and nailed them to the walls of the houses before setting them on fire. Zhenwu Temple is only three miles away from the village, and although there are 30 members of the land and water police stationed at the temple, they dare not come to the rescue due to their weak numbers. As a result, nine out of ten households on the east and west banks of Zhenwu Temple have fled. It is also reported that a large group of 700 to 800 bandits have gathered in the Sanduo Township area of Gaoyou. The extortion of contributions and arson are also occurring there. It is reported that Director Li of the Security Office plans to join forces with the Jiang and Gao counties to launch a large-scale encirclement and suppression operation in the coming days.

Inspection Office Sends Personnel to Search County Junior High School: After the Jiangdu Education Bureau transferred the account books of the junior high school and they were stolen, the case was transferred to the judiciary. Yesterday afternoon (the 2nd), Lu, the prosecutor in charge of the case from the county court's inspection office, along with several judicial police officers, went to Yangxiang Junior High School to conduct a thorough search. It is said that they took away three draft account books from the school. This account is not a proof in the case. The matter of the investigation is a secret and cannot be known to outsiders.

Rugao 87

The Situation in Bingcha is Extremely Critical: The landing of over 400 pirates with weapons in Bingcha has been reported yesterday. Bingcha's 21st district has been completely looted, and more than a dozen men and women have been kidnapped. Today (the 31st), Ya Jia Dai (only about two miles from Bingcha) and Lingzhen have also been looted. It is now reported that the pirates have surrounded Bingcha, and the situation is extremely critical. Yesterday, the Bingcha district office requested reinforcements from Dongtai without success (Bingcha is under the jurisdiction of Dongtai) and then requested aid from the county's first national guard unit and special operations team stationed in Libao. It is reported that the police force set off this morning.

Gaoyou 88

The Verdict on District Chief Xu Cai's Case: Wu Kai, the former chief of the eighth district of this county, was accused by Ding Shen-de and others from Yu Fu Township in the district of intimidation and extortion. After three court hearings, at 7 p.m. yesterday (the 31st), Judge Hu pronounced the verdict. Wu Kai was found guilty of depriving others of their freedom and extortion, and was sentenced to three months in prison and a fine of 200 yuan. The prison sentence was commuted to one day for every two yuan paid.

Jiaxing 89

The Rising Tide of Rickshaw Rental Fees: There are more than ten rickshaw companies in Jiaxing, with a total of over 280 rickshaws in operation each day. Each rickshaw is subject to a daily rental fee of 4 jiao. Recently, some rickshaw pullers requested that the companies reduce the number of rickshaws in operation and were willing to increase the rental fee accordingly. Some companies were receptive to this idea, and as a result, the daily rental fee per rickshaw was increased by 4 fen to 4 jiao 4 fen from November 1st. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 2nd, the majority of the rickshaw pullers refused to work. A small number, driven by the need to earn a living, continued to pull rickshaws on the streets. The majority of the rickshaw pullers, believing that they were not united, ordered them to return their rickshaws and damaged the rickshaws so that they could not be used again. At the same time, they beat up four rickshaw pullers, including Xia. The incident was reported to the Public Security Bureau, which inquired with the rickshaw companies. The companies, realizing that the situation had become strained, denied that they had increased the rental fee. In the afternoon, they issued a notice stating that the rental fee would not be increased. When Dan Dun-san, a judicial officer from the Public Security Bureau, found the rickshaw foreman and informed the rickshaw pullers, urging them to start working immediately and declaring that the rental fee would not be collected that day, the rickshaw pullers were satisfied and immediately began to work. However, it is reported that Xia and others who were beaten and injured will file a lawsuit in court.

Hangzhou 90

Buque Bridge Township Robbed by Bandits: Xiaque Bridge is a major town in Hangzhou County with a thriving market. At 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, five bandit ships suddenly arrived, carrying about 30 bandits armed with wooden-cased guns. After landing, they fired their guns to intimidate the entire town. The seventh police station, overwhelmed by the number of bandits, did not dare to resist, allowing the bandits to search every house for three hours before leaving. The total loss is estimated to be no less than 100,000 yuan. Before leaving, they also kidnapped the respected gentlemen Gao Ruitang, Gao Xulin, and his daughter. The market was left desolate.

Banditry Resurfaces in Taishun: Banditry in Taishun has repeatedly risen and fallen. Since the resignation of the 4th Regiment Commander Gan, yesterday (the 3rd), according to a telegram from citizens in the county, the Zhou bandit gang, after being attacked by the 1st Battalion, fled to the border area between Taishun, Bianyuan, and Shouning. Recently, He Jinbiao, who was offered amnesty, reassembled his remnant forces, uniting over 600 men. The bandits, numbering about 800, have returned and attacked Zhoubin Village and besieged Ruiyang Township. They have reportedly kidnapped over 20 hostages and occupied Shiyang and Yanshan, and are also burning and looting in four directions. Another contingent is stationed in Nanyang, Shouxian, plotting to attack Taizhou City to control the garrison and extort the people. They are extracting civilian wealth by imposing forced loans of silver dollars, committing all kinds of evil. The villagers are fleeing, leaving the late rice crop abandoned. The occupied towns are in imminent danger. After receiving the report, the provincial government immediately telegraphed Zhu, the acting commander of the 4th Regiment, to quickly deploy heavy troops to suppress the bandits and prevent them from entering Ruian and Pingyang counties. At the same time, the provincial government ordered Liu Xiwen, the commander of the 1st Regiment, to transfer the 2nd Battalion from Qingtian to join the attack, ensuring that the bandits are completely eradicated to protect the residents and restore their livelihoods.

Xiaoshan 91

Disputes Over Estimated Rent Collection for Tenant Farms: The agricultural associations of Sihu, Konghu, and other villages in Xiaoshan County have estimated that the average yield of late rice this year is 3.2 shi per mu. Most landowners are dissatisfied because they believe that the harvest this year is abundant and exceeds this amount. The village and neighborhood associations have submitted a report to the county government, based on the farmers' estimated harvest, for record keeping. The county government has rejected the report, stating that the procedure for making a unilateral estimate is not in accordance with regulations. This has led to frequent disputes between farmers and landlords. Recently, both parties have sought guidance from the provincial government, but it is not known how it will be handled.

Funing 92

New County Magistrate Takes Office: Wang Gongxian, the county magistrate of Funing, has resigned due to illness. The provincial government has approved his resignation and appointed Lu Jixi as his successor. Lu arrived in Funing on the 24th and took office on the morning of the 26th.

Expansion of Student Unrest at Jiangsu Agricultural College 95

Students Have Not Yet Returned to Class

Provincial Government Sends Personnel to Investigate Thoroughly

Faculty and Staff Issue Statement

The students of the Second Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural College at Shangjin Bridge outside Tumen protested over food issues around 7:00 a.m. on October 31st, leading to a class strike by the entire student body against Dean of Studies Dai Qixiang. On the previous day (the 1st), the students of the First Agricultural College organized a support association. The students of the Second Agricultural College also went on strike and distributed official statements. If the goal of expelling Dai Qixiang is not achieved, they will not return to class. The strike has therefore expanded. Principal Liao Jianan went to the provincial capital on the morning of the 2nd to meet with the Director of the Education Department to request instructions. Principal Liao returned to Suzhou by car yesterday (the 3rd). After arriving in the provincial capital, Principal Liao went to the provincial government, the provincial party headquarters, and the Education Department to present the entire situation, stating that the student unrest was actually a minor matter that had been amplified by organization. Because Principal Liao reported this way, the provincial government decided to send personnel to Suzhou to conduct a thorough investigation. Yesterday (the 3rd), a special telegram was sent to Huang, the county magistrate of Wuxian County, ordering him to go to investigate the matter and report back for review. (Statement from Faculty and Staff)

The preparatory students of the Second Branch of our school suddenly used throwing bowls at the dining hall during breakfast on October 31st as a signal. They swarmed to the office of Preparatory Dean Dai Qiyang, dragged Dai out, and beat him all the way out of the school with fists and kicks (his arms, knees, face, and waist were bruised and swollen, and he had a high fever). They then closed the school gates and posted slogans, shouting many outrageous slogans. At that time, the principal and dean of studies heard the news and tried to stop them, but they refused to listen. After gathering them for a discussion and earnestly explaining the situation and asking them about the cause of the incident, the students were unable to answer and instead shouted loudly and behaved unreasonably, as if they were drinking mad medicine. The commotion continued until late at night. The next day at dawn, they swarmed to the first branch of the university in an attempt to coerce students into joining them. The undergraduate students were not moved and continued to attend classes as usual. The preparatory students then broke into the classrooms, forcibly dragging the teachers out and demonstrating to the undergraduate students. If anyone tried to reason with them, they would try to beat them. The barbarity of these students is truly heartbreaking. The Second Branch of our school is located near Tumen, and the preparatory students have very little self-control. Dean Dai has always been strict in his management in order to protect the young people, which is also his responsibility, but he did not realize that this would lead to resentment. The cause of the incident lies in this. Their unreasonable behavior is truly lamentable. The students beat Dean Dai for his conscientious management, and they tried to beat the faculty and staff for their advice and guidance. They tried to beat the faculty and students of the First Branch for attending classes. Such acts of violence put everyone in danger. We, the faculty and staff, unanimously urge the principal to investigate the leaders of this riot, punish them severely according to the school regulations, and take effective measures to protect the safety of the faculty and staff. We will temporarily do our best to maintain the school and support the principal. We hereby declare this in the hope that it will be publicly recognized.

Local News

Foreigners Invade Educational Authority 97

The Municipal Council Establishes an Education Department

Sets a Deadline for All Schools to Submit Reports

Will Prohibit the Teaching of Party Doctrines

The Party Headquarters Has Strongly Opposed It

Riri News states that there are a total of 93 municipal and private primary schools in the Shanghai Municipal Council's Public Settlement, according to a survey conducted in May of this year. As of now, the number is even higher. There are also more than ten private primary schools run by foreigners. Previously, the Municipal Education Bureau planned to bring the primary schools run by foreigners under control in order to unify education in the city. After hearing this news, the Municipal Council immediately investigated the Chinese primary schools in the settlement and issued a form to each school, setting a deadline of the end of December for the detailed submission of information about the school, such as the principal, professors, students, funding, and tuition fees. At the same time, the Municipal Council established an Education Department to manage all matters related to schools in the settlement and has planned to ban the teaching of the Three Principles of the People in schools after they are all managed by the Municipal Council's Education Department. It will also increase the number of religious courses. Recently, after receiving this order and the form to be filled out, some weak schools have filled out the form according to the requirements, while others have opposed the foreigners' invasion of our country's educational authority and ignored it. They have also reported the situation to the party headquarters in each district for verification. The party headquarters in the third and fourth districts held meetings to discuss the matter and have decided on the following countermeasures: (1) Order all schools to refuse to fill out the report form; (2) Submit a request to the government to seriously negotiate with the Municipal Council. After receiving this notice, all schools have unanimously complied with the first point, it is said.

Shanghai South District Education Federation

Academic Lectures and General Assembly 102

Attended by over 400 people from more than 30 schools

The Shanghai Southern District Municipal School Teachers' Association held an academic lecture and its general assembly yesterday, the 3rd, at 1:30 PM at the Wuben Girls' School. Over 400 people from more than 30 schools attended. Zhao Luqing, Qian Xuanqing, and Chen Pingyi were publicly elected as chairpersons, and Xu Peihang and Xu Tongqian were selected as recorders. After the salutation, the chairperson reported that today's event was both the Shanghai Southern District Teachers' Association general assembly and an academic lecture. He said, "We, as municipal school teachers in the southern district of Shanghai, bear a heavy responsibility and should constantly study and seek advancement. Today's assembly and lecture can be said to address both aspects."

Academic Lecture: The lecturers, Mr. Cen Dezhang, Mr. Dong Renjian, and Mr. Fang Xun'guang, have been invited. First, please welcome lecturer Mr. Cen. Mr. Cen said, "I dare not call this a problem-solving lecture. Since we are all colleagues, I might as well speak frankly about the hardships. I often have thoughts about the scope of education. Is the teacher's responsibility only to teach students, and does it end there? Regarding those who consider themselves outside the scope of education, the problem with people is their fondness for being teachers. I believe the problem isn't liking to be a teacher, but being unwilling to be a student after becoming a teacher. Educators are busy all day, exhausting their energy, and can only barely fulfill the duties of a teacher. However, the world's knowledge is advancing rapidly. If we remain the same as when we were students, or if we teach for ten years and remain unchanged, what will the result be? It's easy to imagine. Teachers who want to improve themselves face obstacles in their environment, such as their livelihood, the school, and society. Their living conditions are difficult, and their salaries are meager, forcing them to seek self-sufficiency. Schools often focus their resources on students and neglect the teachers' professional development. Even if teachers want to advance themselves, they lack the resources. Society's perception of teachers is weak, and even if they strive for advancement, they are not valued. A perfunctory attitude arises as a result, causing this precious quality to be lost. A teacher should both teach students and pursue knowledge, so that their own knowledge constantly advances and those being taught also improve daily. This would be a blessing for society." Next, Mr. Dong Renjian lectured on the "Life Path of Education" (A) Education (Education is a specialized field), not a temporary job. In primitive times, there was no division of labor. Later, education became established and advanced into a specialized field. However, the level of specialization among teachers is not as high as in fields like medicine and law, with primary school teachers being the most highly valued in terms of professional competence. (B) Specialized Education: Modern education is based on scientific principles, utilizing stable sciences such as psychology, education, sociology, and economics to aid in education. By 1920, primary education had become truly professionalized. After 1920, secondary education gradually became professionalized, and in the future, universities will likely follow suit. (C) (The Life Path of Education) What is the current state of education in China? We can understand this from the number of children attending school, students' academic performance, and the living conditions of teachers. Educators should be educated, but not separated from other areas like politics and economics. However, the focus must always be on education. Therefore, schools can be specialized, but they cannot completely forget their educational purpose. Education is about humanization, which cannot be ignored. In summary, to seek the professionalization of education and a life path: (1) Teachers should act professionally and not forget that education is a profession. (2) Schools are professional institutions. While they may discuss politics and economics, they should fundamentally focus on education. (3) Education is a developing profession, not a tool for personal gain. In the current professional situation, universities are the last to change. Finally, Mr. Fang Xun'guang lectured on (New Standards for Phonetic Symbols and National Pronunciation). After the lecture, the general assembly was held.

General Assembly: The general assembly was still chaired by Qian Xuanqing, Zhao Luqing, and Chen Pingyi. Representatives Zhu Ya'kui from the Municipal Party Department and Li Dachao from the Municipal Education Bureau were invited to provide guidance, limiting the discussion to (1) an amendment to the association's constitution, which was approved; (2) the election of supervisory committee members. Qian Xuanqing, Li Bojun, Xi Anzhai, Xu Peihang, Xu Zhenxia, Zhao Luqing, Xu Tongqian, Wang Weiru, Hu Huaitian, Huang Tieya, Xu Pinren, Xu Zhilin, Qian Cijiu, Xu Liaohua, and Gu Yinqian were elected as executive committee members. Bao Yuxueyao, Hou Zhoujinji, Wang Dingcheng, and Yao Jiji were nominated as alternate executive committee members. Wu Bokang, Ju Xinghong, Wang Beiwu, Yu Jiu, Shi Baihu, Huang Zhuang, Zou Yinlu, Lu Hanqiu, and Cao Junruo were elected as supervisory committee members. Luo Lin, Zhang Qidong, and Huang Shengbai were nominated as alternate supervisory committee members. (3) A request to the Education Bureau to organize an out-of-town tour for teachers and staff was approved and handed over to the executive committee to handle. (4) A request to the Education Bureau to establish a phonetic symbol training institute: Education Bureau representative Li Dachao reported that the bureau had already begun preparations for this. The issue was not discussed. (5) How to handle the remaining funds from the previous Joint Association: Reserved. (6) A request to the Education Bureau to issue a registration certificate for the association was approved and handed over to the executive committee to handle. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM.

| Review in the Morning Today | Third General Assembly in the Afternoon |

Policies for Developing China's Industry and Commerce - Zhu Tongjiu

Agriculture, industry, and commerce are the foundation of a country's economic organization. The three are equally important and should not be harmed. If a country is rich in natural resources, it should utilize its natural resources to develop agriculture, industry, and commerce simultaneously, as in the United States. If a country is unfortunately limited by its land area, it should develop its unique strengths to compensate for the deficiencies, as in England. This is the principle of applied economics, and no one would dare to deny it.

China has a vast territory and abundant natural resources. In principle, agriculture, industry, and commerce should be developed simultaneously. However, the reality is far from this. Regarding agriculture, grain shortages frequently reach our ears. This year, the import of foreign rice amounted to millions of stones. China, known to the world for its agricultural base, relies on foreign countries for its grain supply. It is both pitiful and ridiculous to say. For now, let us leave agriculture aside and talk about industry and commerce. The stagnation of industry and commerce remains the same. Foreign goods flood the market, while domestic goods are as rare as morning stars. China's market is almost entirely occupied by foreign goods. The economic losses for China each year amount to no less than tens of millions. Regarding commerce, the power of finance is firmly controlled by foreigners. Even in the major trading ports, most of the import and export trade is controlled by foreign merchants. Chinese merchants are only responsible for errands and eat the leftovers. How can we speak of flourishing commerce?

Now that the National Industry and Commerce Conference has convened, I will present some strategies for developing China's industry and commerce, based on what I have seen and heard, for the reference of China's industrial and commercial giants. Please find them detailed below:

1. Protective Tariff Policy: China's tariffs have been unable to be independent for years due to the constraints of unequal treaties. The destruction of China's nascent industries by foreigners is due to this. Although we can now implement tariff autonomy, the tax rates are still determined by agreement and cannot be said to be completely free. Therefore, protecting domestic nascent industries is still not allowed in practice. If we want to develop industry today, it is necessary to implement complete tariff autonomy. This is the first point. In addition to the method of protection, the Chinese government must also encourage the export of domestic goods. The method of encouragement is what Mr. Yu Qiaqing proposed: (Exempting domestic goods from export tax and abolishing the tax exemption and tax payment methods for foreign goods.) This will reduce the cost of domestic goods and make it easier to sell them in foreign markets. Secondly, it will increase the price of foreign goods and reduce their sales in the country. The method is good and beautiful, achieving two benefits with one move. This is the second point.

Increased costs of industrial products lead to higher prices, which affects sales. From the consumer's point of view, foreign goods are well-made and their prices are not much different from domestic goods. Therefore, people tend to buy foreign goods. As a result, domestic goods are not easy to sell due to their high prices. Therefore, the heavy miscellaneous taxes in the interior directly increase the cost of industrial products and indirectly increase prices, resulting in losses due to poor sales. The ruthless miscellaneous taxes in the interior should be reduced as appropriate.

3. Promoting Transportation and Road Construction: It is well known that transportation in China is not very convenient, and transportation infrastructure cannot be called developed. Therefore, inland goods (raw materials) are not easily transported out to supply various factories. As a result, there are complaints about goods being abandoned in the inland, and factories lament the lack of raw materials. Under this kind of indifferent state, how can industry and commerce develop? This is the first point. Since inland raw materials are not easily transported out, the purchasing power of the inland people is low and they naturally cannot afford to buy industrial products from outside. As a result, the sales of domestic goods are affected. This is the second point. Since the transportation industry is not developed, transportation must be very inconvenient and the cost of transportation must be very high. Even if some industries are transported to the inland, their prices will be high. How can the farmers in the inland, who have low living costs, afford to buy them? This is the third point. With these three factors, the industrial products of the industrial and commercial centers cannot be transported into the inland for sale, and the original sales in the inland cannot be transported out to supply factories. This is a real obstacle to the future of industry and commerce. The only way to eliminate this obstacle is to promote transportation and road construction. 4. Improving Labor Treatment and Preventing Labor Strikes: In recent years, labor strikes have surged, and strikes are often heard. The reason is that labor treatment is too low, leading to livelihood problems. I believe that rather than reducing production due to labor strikes, it is better to increase wages to increase production efficiency, so that the industrial sector can do its best to produce, and the commercial sector can also buy and sell. The prosperity of industry and commerce depends on this. 5. Supporting Existing Domestic Industries to Prevent Foreign Merchants' Encroachment and Mergers: Existing domestic industries are often encroached upon or merged by foreign merchants with strong capital due to their small scale and limited capital. For example, in the match industry, Swedish merchants use their strong capital and trust methods to merge with them. The future of China's match industry is in imminent danger. I think that existing industries urgently need to be protected and maintained. The emergency method is that Mr. Liu Hongsheng, a member of the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association, proposed a method of merging and operating similar industries, which can remedy the situation. The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association may announce it soon, so I will not repeat it.

6. Eradicating Banditry: In recent years, there have been many bandits in the interior of China, making travel inconvenient and merchants hesitant. This is a major obstacle to the future of domestic commerce in China. I think that for the sake of developing domestic commerce, the central government should carry out a clearing campaign after the military is over to eradicate bandits and communists in order to remove obstacles. Whether or not this will be implemented is the responsibility of the government, but the responsibility of requesting it lies with the Industry and Commerce Conference.

7. Protection for the Industrial and Commercial Sectors: Since the establishment of the Republic of China, there has not been a year without war in the country, and before and after the war, the source of war funds has mostly come from the industrial and commercial sectors. Before the war broke out, the industrial and commercial sectors shouldered a portion of the military expenses. Winning the war is good, but losing the war would result in local extortion and a complete wipeout. After the new army arrived, it would be necessary to prepare funds to welcome them. Again and again, how can the capital of the industrial and commercial sectors not be exhausted? In addition, after the war ended, the local area suffered and the market was depressed. How can industry and commerce not decline? This is the first point. In recent years, the biggest problem in the country is the large number of soldiers. With many soldiers, it is difficult to raise funds. Therefore, many armies raise funds in their stationed areas. Industrial and commercial enterprises with a larger scale are often patronized by Mr. Qiuba. Therefore, almost all factories and merchants, large and small, are in a state of anxiety. This is the second point. Taking into account the above two situations, both are fatal injuries to the future development of industry and commerce. I think the central government should plan for the aftermath to protect the industrial and commercial sectors. In summary, the above (1), (2), (6), and (7) are the responsibility of the government, and (3), (4), and (5) are the responsibility of the industrial and commercial sectors themselves. I sincerely hope that the Industry and Commerce Conference will find a way to improve the future, so that the future of industry and commerce in our country may have a chance.

Discussion of the Situation of Each Case

(Passed) Case 1: Submitted by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for Discussion 113

Proposal on Joint Domestic Industry and Commerce Operations (Review Opinion) This case is needed by the times, but it concerns the industrial and commercial circles themselves. It is proposed that the General Assembly discuss it.

The Counselor of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce reported on the content of this case and asked the members to discuss it. (Discussion) Liu Hongsheng reported on the situation of the Swedish merchants' Ruizhong Match Company suppressing Chinese merchants. I once united three match companies to handle the match business, and its performance was better than the three companies handling it separately. It can also concentrate capital and talents to compete with foreign merchants. Therefore, I absolutely agree with this case. Hu Shuhua seconded the motion and asked the chairman to put it to a vote. Wang Jie'an advocated that the Ministry issue an order to the various chambers of commerce for implementation. Wang Yunwu said that the effectiveness of the method requires detailed research and investigation. Germany once established this institution with 6,000 experts. Therefore, this case should be researched by an agency jointly organized by the industrial and commercial circles and the government to make the implementation of this plan more effective. The chairman advocated that after this case is passed, Wang Yunwu should submit another proposal for discussion. (Passed)

(Passed) Case 22 (Proposal on Prohibiting the Export of Factory Sand and Waste Iron) 115

The original proposer, Hu Shuhua, reported on the content of this case. All principles in the first article, which stated that the government should issue a clear order prohibiting the export of iron, have been reviewed and passed. The second article stated that the competent authorities should set the price method when domestic steel and iron factories purchase iron sand and waste iron. The original proposer withdrew. Shi Ying said that the situation of Hubei mining sand being sold to the Japanese-run Yangtze Machinery Company is very important. I once advocated prohibiting exports. Ding Jingchen said that the prohibition of the export of waste iron and iron sand must be specified in detail. China's current steel and iron needs are all supplied by foreigners. I advocate using tariffs to increase the prohibition of iron exports. Lu Chengzhang said that China's iron ore, first of all, Muye Ping Dazhi and Taiping Mine in Anhui, are all related to Japan. If this case is passed, then those not related to the Japanese will be prohibited from exporting, thus suspending operations. I advocate formulating another method. Wang Ruoxi reported on the situation of the iron ore in Dongshan Province being controlled by the Japanese. Wu Jian said that the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining had long planned to limit the method for this case, but the Ministry of Finance opposed the iron sand export tax increase method. I advocate that the government set up a special agency to set the price. Fang said that I oppose abolishing the iron sand export policy and should stipulate that if there is a surplus of iron needed in the country, it can be exported. Pan Xulun advocated that this case (should be reviewed and handled by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining) (majority passed).

Case No. 27 (Eliminate Foreign Enterprises in China to Resist Economic Aggression) 116

| Resubmit for Detailed Review and Formulation of Measures | Wang Jie’an and Ma Ze Zhao Advocate Restricting Foreigners’ Development of Industries in China. Case No. 27: Eliminate Foreign Enterprises in China to Resist Economic Aggression. First, the original proposer, Zhu Bin Yuan, reported on the intention of the case, but the measures were slightly inadequate. He requested the assembly to discuss. Wang Ruoxi stated that foreign factories could create skilled workers and other benefits for China, but under considerable conditions, foreigners should be encouraged to establish factories in China. When China has sufficient strength, then elimination can be considered. Li Quanshi stated that during the review, the phrase "eliminate" in this case was changed to "restrict," and restrictions were imposed through registration and licensing measures. (Detailed review opinions can be found in yesterday's newspaper). Ma Ze Zhao stated that the Japanese are vigorously developing the textile industry in China, which affects the development of China's cotton yarn industry. Therefore, he advocated that foreign enterprises should be restricted. Xu Ji stated that the root of the problem can only be resolved after the abolition of unequal treaties. This case can be resubmitted to the review committee for detailed formulation of measures before being resubmitted to the assembly for discussion. The Chairman reported that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce should register and restrict foreign businesses in China at the Chinese government office. Future regulations in the industrial and commercial laws should be detailed to ensure that foreigners adhere to the scope of business. Yang Xingfo stated that the assembly has very little time. To save time, if there are no questions, the original proposer does not need to report. A separate case can be established to thoroughly study and discuss the matter of foreign industries in China. Wang Jie'an stated that foreigners have strong financial resources, which hinders the development of Chinese industries. Therefore, he advocated that restrictions should be imposed appropriately. It was resolved that the case should be submitted to the review committee for detailed formulation of measures. If members have opinions, they can submit them in writing to the review committee or participate in the review committee.
