Public Concession Dog Racing Track

Soon to be Completely Prohibited 182

According to the "Great American Evening Post", the British Consulate and the Municipal Council authorities have decided on the fate of Shanghai's dog racing venues. This morning (the 3rd), the British Consul-General, Mr. Brenan, the Chairman of the Municipal Council, Mr. Fessenden, and the Chief of Police, Mr. Read, met to decide that their aim is not only to suppress, but to completely prohibit it. All the members of the Municipal Council also agree with this move. This morning, a reporter specifically visited the British Consul-General, who stated that the British authorities do not approve of dog racing in Shanghai. If the Municipal Council takes measures to ban it, they will provide full assistance, as dog racing undoubtedly increases crime in the concession. Those who gamble large sums in dog racing venues often lose huge amounts of money and are driven to commit crimes. Therefore, it is necessary to prohibit dog racing. The decision on this matter was made at a meeting in the Consul-General's office this morning, and the Municipal Council is currently considering the methods. It is expected that the ban will be submitted for discussion at the next Council meeting and will be passed. During this morning's meeting, Mr. Fessenden and Mr. Read both expressed their opinions on dog racing and the position of the Municipal Council, requesting the Consul-General and the British authorities to support the closure of the dog racing venues. Mr. Brenan also explained the position of the British authorities and guaranteed their support. Subsequently, the reporter inquired whether a concrete plan had been agreed upon. Mr. Brenan replied that no plan had been agreed upon yet, and that the matter would be handled by the Municipal Council. He also stated that the two dog racing venues in the Public Concession are operated by British merchants. When they were first established, the British authorities did not expect the gambling craze to be so intense, nor did they expect that those who lost heavily in dog racing venues would engage in embezzlement and theft, leading to an increase in crime to today's level. Finally, when asked whether horse racing would also be banned, the British Consul-General replied that Mr. Fessenden and others did not mention this matter when they met at the consulate today. Subsequently, the reporter met with Mr. Fessenden, who stated that the prohibition of dog racing is inevitable, but the method still needs to be decided in the next Council meeting. Moreover, an official of the Municipal Council said that not only do the consuls oppose dog racing, but all the members of the Municipal Council also believe that dog racing is not in the interest of the citizens. Furthermore, according to Mr. Brenan and Mr. Fessenden, although the British authorities and the Municipal Council have decided to prohibit dog racing, they have no intention of making things difficult for the dog racing venues. Once a plan is decided, they will be given ample time to wind up their business.

Inside the City God Temple

Apprentice Beats Owner to Death 183

Apprentice Flees in Fear of Punishment

Owner's Wife Cries Madly

Lei Sheng-sheng, a 57-year-old man from Suzhou, had some savings and opened three porcelain shops in the City God Temple inside the Little East Gate. One was named Lei Ren Ji, and another Ren Chang. Lei Ren Ji, located near the old site of Osmanthus Hall, hired an apprentice named Xu De-xiang from Zhenjiang, who was 21 years old and earned nine yuan a month. However, he was rude and often resorted to violence, acting like a hooligan. Lei Sheng-sheng repeatedly reprimanded him but to no avail, and fearing trouble, continued to employ him. It is known that yesterday morning at 8:30, Lei Sheng-sheng went to the shop from his home at No. 2 Hongfu Lane, Fangbang Road, as usual, and Xu De-xiang happened to enter from outside. When asked why he had gone out, he initially did not respond. Lei Sheng-sheng scolded him slightly, and Xu De-xiang dared to roar and jump, directly attacking Lei Sheng-sheng. Lei, being old and weak, was no match for him and immediately fell to the ground. Xu De-xiang forcefully struck Lei Sheng-sheng's head with his palm. The nerves in his head were excessively stimulated, and his complexion became pale, his breathing weak. The area struck was split open, and red blood flowed continuously. Seeing the situation was bad, Xu De-xiang took the opportunity to escape. He shouted loudly to the other shop assistants, opened his feet, and fled towards Yu Garden Road, not knowing where he was going. The injured Lei Sheng-sheng was unconscious and was carried back to Hongfu Lane by his family. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died at 11 a.m. They immediately reported to the police station and the local authorities, requesting an autopsy and the arrest of the murderer to avenge the wrong. It is said that Xu De-xiang's guarantor, a Mr. Xu, has also escaped and his whereabouts are unknown. Lei Sheng-sheng left behind three sons: Wei-xing, 17 years old; Gen-xing, 13 years old; and the youngest, A-san, 9 years old. He also had one daughter who was still in her swaddling clothes. His wife, upon seeing her husband's violent death yesterday, cried uncontrollably, as if she had gone mad. (Shanghai South Society)

Director Weidebang Missing 185

Went Missing on the "Dalian Maru" Ship Approaching Shanghai

According to the "Great American Evening Post", Mr. Weidebang, the managing director of Biefa Foreign Firm, went to the three northeastern provinces for sightseeing. He took the "Dalian Maru" back to Shanghai a few days ago. On Saturday (the 1st), when the ship was outside the mouth of the Yangtze River, seven hours away from Shanghai, he suddenly went missing. The truth of the matter remains unknown. Initially, it was suspected that he had committed suicide by jumping into the sea, but according to his friends and colleagues in the foreign firm, it was likely an accidental fall into the sea. Although Mr. Wei's health was not very good, he would not have committed suicide for this reason. Moreover, he was always optimistic and had not married, so he had no family worries or financial burdens. Therefore, it is not believed that he had a desire to renounce the world and jump into the sea. It is said that Mr. Wei's disappearance was first discovered by a Chinese gentleman in the same cabin. Mr. Wei got up very early, had breakfast, and then went for a walk on the deck. Later, the gentleman wanted to find Mr. Wei but could not find him anywhere. He reported it to the captain, who searched the entire ship but found no trace of him. After arriving in Shanghai, he reported it to the police station, who inspected his luggage but found no clues. In addition to 422 yuan in cash and a HSBC bank passbook, there were no important items in his suitcase. Mr. Wei was born in England and was 50 years old.

Page 16

Rushing to Board the Ferry

Twenty to Thirty Female Workers Fall into the River 186

Many Rescued

Quite a Few Drowned

The Xinfashun small steamship of Fuxing Company mainly tows barges and ships in the dock. When free, it picks up passengers at the Qichang pier in Pudong and the Weisaigong pier in Hudong. Each fare is four copper coins for male passengers and half for female passengers. The ship is very small and can only hold fifty or sixty people. At about 6 o'clock yesterday morning, it was picking up passengers at the Pudong pier. At that time, there were sixty or seventy female workers who worked in various cigarette factories in Hudong and lived in Pudong. Because the factory opened at 7 o'clock, they were eager to board the ferry to enter the factory. They rushed to board the ferry, ignoring the danger. However, the side of the ship could not withstand the pressure of so many people and tilted slightly inward. The female workers, who had not yet stood firmly, immediately fell into the river, about twenty to thirty of them. The sailors, seeing the disaster, rushed forward to rescue them, rescuing more than ten people on the spot. The Yaofuji dredging ship, which was parked there, also helped to rescue more than ten people. Those rescued were like drowned chickens, and the weather was very cold at that time. The wind blew, and everyone shivered and had no color. However, they had no clothes to change and could only run home to change. Those who were not rescued in time suffered a tragic drowning. Because people did not have time to pay attention to the number of people who fell into the water, the details could not be confirmed. When asked, nearby boatmen said that at least five or six people died. A hunched old woman, about fifty years old, suddenly ran to the pier where the accident occurred and cried loudly, looking at the river. She left in the evening. According to her, she had three daughters, the eldest was 22 years old, the second was 20 years old, and the youngest was 18 years old. The two youngest daughters were rescued and returned home. The eldest daughter was buried in the bottom of the river, etc. It was also said to be tragic. After the accident, Mr. Hu Yufu, the manager of the small steamship, reported the case to the water police station for the record. Chen Ashi, the foreman, was interrogated by the water patrol team to determine the situation and to judge the responsibility. At the same time, the water police station, upon hearing the news, also sent detectives Wang Haiquan and Hu Changqing to rush to the scene and detained the Xinfashun small steamship for investigation.

Capital Police Department Hires Firefighting Specialists 187

Since Police Chief Wu of the Capital Police Department took office, he has been actively working on public security matters. He has paid even more attention to firefighting, as the quality of fire administration is closely related to the people. He is seeking to improve it in order to make it complete. Therefore, he commissioned Section Chief Xie Guanyi of the Security Section to come to Shanghai with the members of the districts and bureaus of the capital to inspect the fire brigades in the Chinese districts and visit the concessions to see the police administration and various firefighting equipment. They were very detailed and praised the arrangements and all the measures as being comparable to those in the concessions. Therefore, he felt that only specialists could effectively manage fire administration. Chief Wu expressed great sympathy and immediately ordered Mr. Xie to write a letter to the South and West District Fire Brigades in Shanghai, proposing to hire Director Xia Guoliang to go to the capital to serve as the captain of the team and manage firefighting matters. And if he could not spare the time, he should recommend suitable talents and select two qualified squad leaders to act on his behalf. Director Xia, because he was busy with public and private affairs in Shanghai, could not accept the position and immediately recommended Mr. Wang Haici, a member of the local council, who was experienced and talented and could take on the position. For squad leaders, he recommended Mr. Zhu Zilian, a volunteer member of this district, and Mr. Yang Zhenmin, a clerk in the East District. Therefore, letters and telegrams were exchanged and a compromise was reached. Yesterday afternoon, a letter was received from Section Chief Xie, urging Mr. Wang Haici to go to the capital as soon as possible.

Pirates Rampant Outside Wusongkou 189

Pirates Land and Occupy Civilian Houses

Water and Land Police Corps Sent to Suppress

Recently, a large group of pirates suddenly sailed three or more pirate ships to the waters outside Wusongkou, such as Fengli Juegang. They surrounded four large and small fishing boats fishing in the waters, looted them successfully, and then set the ships on fire. Most of the crew members fell into the water and died. The pirates then landed at Beixingqiao Port and carried out large-scale looting. The residents of the area knew that they would be harmed if the pirates landed, so they abandoned their homes in haste and fled elsewhere, and sent people to report to the Juegang water and land police team. It is now known that the pirates have occupied civilian houses since landing and have not left yet. Juegang is very close and the situation is extremely urgent. The water and land police team and the local defense force have been sent to suppress them.

Foreigner Commits Robbery 193

Searches the Store Owner's Person But Finds Nothing

Opens Fire with Handgun Fortunately No One is Injured

Yesterday afternoon at about 6 o'clock, a blue-eyed man, whose nationality was unknown, suddenly came to the Ruì Tài Woolen Shop at No. 616 Nanjing Road while it was still open for business. Speaking in English, he rushed upstairs to search the store owner's person, but found nothing. He wanted to rummage through the boxes and cabinets, but the store assistants downstairs, seeing the situation, knew that he must be a thief and shouted loudly. An apprentice went out the back door to call for the police. The Western thief, seeing this, immediately took out a handgun from his sleeve and fired a shot, fortunately without injuring anyone. He then fled out the door. By the time the police arrived, the thief was nowhere to be found. Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to the police station, requesting an investigation.

Shi A'gen is Stabbed 194

Life in Danger

Shi A'gen, a 47-year-old man from Chongming, runs a stove shop at No. 979 Huayi Fang, North Sichuan Road. Yesterday afternoon at a little past one o'clock, two men wearing short coats suddenly came and asked Shi if there was anyone upstairs. Before A'gen could answer, one of them pulled out a sharp axe from his arms and struck A'gen's left temple, causing blood to flow profusely. The assailant then ran away wildly. The upstairs is rented to a Cantonese who runs a small general association and employs a tea server from Yangzhou named Ayou, who is about 20 years old, looks like Pan An, and is naturally frivolous. He often joked with his wife and has been reprimanded by me several times, so he has not spoken to me for many days. I was ambushed this time, perhaps at the instigation of Ayou.

Strange Child with Cat Face and Human Body 195

Hanging High on a Tree Branch in a Hemp Sack

Villagers Break Superstition The Public Does Not Reincarnate

A hemp sack was hanging on a big tree along the river west of the Catholic Church Street in Xujiahui, Shanghai West, yesterday morning. A villager passing by noticed that the sack was quite heavy and wanted to find out what it was, so he took the sack down and opened it. It was a strange child. The body and limbs were like a normal child, but the head was round, the face was round, the eyes were round and black, the teeth were all bent, and the ears, nose, and mouth were all like a wildcat. The villager thought that if he had a strange child at home, everyone would come to see it, so that he would not be reborn. Therefore, the child must have been abandoned here by a nearby family. A crowd gathered at once, all saying that it was a child with a cat face and a human body. In the evening, someone moved the strange child and buried it in the mud.

When People's Organizations Gather

Should Implement People's Rights Initiative 200

The Municipal Public Training Association Is Ordered to Inform

The Public Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang issued a circular to the people's organizations in this city yesterday, stating that the Central Executive Committee issued instruction No. 16746, stating that investigating and starting training the people in the use of the four powers is the party's most important task today. The prerequisite for using the four powers is to make the people familiar with the use of people's rights initiatives. All organs, schools, and groups should first be familiar with people's rights initiatives in order to set an example for the people to use the four powers. Recently, it has been found that many groups affiliated with the party hold various gatherings, and many of them can follow people's rights initiatives, but there are also some who are not familiar with the order and are disordered, which not only wastes time and reduces effectiveness, but also indirectly hinders the completion of the training period. For this reason, in addition to informing the National Government to order its subordinates to implement it, this order specially orders the association to comply and order its affiliated groups to implement people's rights initiatives when holding gatherings in order to train and achieve practical results. This is very important.

Two River Steamship Fire Notes 201

Lianhe Steamboat's Carelessness

The Changjiang steamboat Lianhe of Yihua Foreign Company was returning to Shanghai from Mo Xia this time. When the boat was about to arrive in Nanjing, the wires in its fire cabin suddenly short-circuited, and a raging fire broke out. The fire spread to the cargo hold. The shipowner learned about it and immediately stopped the boat and ordered all the crew and sailors to put out the fire with all their might. Only then did the fire extinguish, but the goods in the cabin, except for those burned on the surface, were all water-stained. They were now unloaded at the Shuntai wharf, and public appraisers will be sent today to inspect the loss and notify the customers to pay the water fee. As for the ship, it has been slightly damaged and has been sent for repair. The passengers and crew were not harmed.

Hongyuan Barge Fire

The Changjiang steamboat Hongyuan of Sanbei Company was dragging two barges loaded with 15,100 yards of Texaco kerosene from Shanghai to Hankou this time. When loading at the dock, the kerosene loaded in one of the barges was suddenly ignited by a cigarette butt, and the oil was flammable, so it spread rapidly. Fortunately, the dock was full, so it was easier to put out the fire. As a result, more than 200 boxes were burned, but the ship was not seriously damaged. The cargo owner and the insurance company were immediately notified for inspection.

Brief Biography of Mr. Murai, the Incoming Japanese Consul 202

Since Shanghai's Japanese Consul General, Minister Plenipotentiary Shigemitsu Kui, left his post, there have been reports that the Japanese government is now planning to appoint Mr. Murai Kuraso to succeed him. Mr. Murai graduated from Tokyo Higher Commercial School in 1911 and came to China to teach at the East Asia Common Culture Academy in this city. In 1914, he passed the diplomatic examination and served in Harbin, Xiangshan, New York and other ports. In 1919, he was transferred to the Beijing Legation as a third-class secretary, and the following year, he was promoted to official and transferred to the Fourth Asian Bureau. In 1924, he was appointed as a second-class secretary at the London Embassy and later promoted to first class. In November 1926, he was appointed as the chief of the First Section of the Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. In February 1928, he became the consul-general in Kolkata. He is now scheduled to be transferred to Shanghai.

Discussion on Pay Increase for Taikoo Seamen 203

Yesterday, Taikoo Navigation Company sent a letter to the Seamen's General Union along with a proposed pay increase contract for seamen. (Contract) The contract established between Taikoo Company in Shanghai and the Chinese Seamen's Union is listed on the left: (1) Starting November 1, 1930, Taikoo Navigation Company in Shanghai will increase the monthly salary of cooks, sailors, and stewards on each ship by four yuan, but the current rice subsidy of two yuan per month will be cancelled on the same day. (2) No further pay increases will be made. (3) The Seamen's Union will endeavor to assist Taikoo Navigation Company in conducting and developing its business. (4) After the two contracts are signed, one copy will be kept by the Seamen's Union and one copy will be kept by Taikoo Company. (5) The contract will take effect from the date of signing. After receiving this draft contract and letter, the Seamen's General Union held a meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss the results. The following points need to be modified in the proposed contract (counterproposal): (1) The Seamen's Union and Taikoo Company should be listed together. (2) The 19th year of the Republic of China and the Gregorian calendar year 1930 should also be listed together. (3) The pay increase starting from November 1 should be changed to a pay increase starting from September 1. (4) The clause "No further pay increases will be made" should be completely removed. It is determined that a letter will be sent to Taikoo Company today (the 4th) to reply.

Plea for National Coal to Be Allowed to Leave the Mines 204

Qingdao Railway Cancels Half-Price Freight

Yesterday, the China National Coal Production and Sales Association received a letter from Qingdao coal merchants stating (excerpt omitted): Since the Railway Bureau, under the pretext of relieving the coal shortage in Qingdao, cancelled the half-price export freight, more than a month has passed without restoration. As a result, except for small batches loaded for export by Japanese merchants, no Chinese coal merchant has loaded a single ton. The Railway Bureau declared that it cancelled the half-price to restrict external transport in order to relieve the coal shortage. However, it is not known that this year's export volume is more than half less than in previous years. The reason is that since this spring, either there has been a lack of wagons, or military events have occurred, disrupting transportation. The coal shortage in Qingdao was entirely caused by the interruption of the railway. Now that the coal shortage has become a thing of the past, the coal reserves in various inland stations and Qingdao are very sufficient, so the coal price is falling daily. If the half-price is not restored to allow exports, the coal mines in Zibo and Zhangqiu counties will inevitably have to close completely. The Railway Bureau still stubbornly refuses to restore it, and its ulterior motives are conceivable. Its destruction and oppression of coal merchants are deeply resented. Now, the Chinese authorities advocate industry and protect domestic goods, fearing it is already too late. How can they continue to destroy? This is a brief account, please urge the conference to find a way out for coal merchants (rest omitted).

Social News

Arriving in Jinan 218

— Moye

Jinan Correspondence

For two days after arriving in Jinan, the weather has been continuously rainy and depressing. There is no military news to report. As for the suffering of the people, due to the lack of statistical materials, it is difficult to obtain concrete content. I would like to talk about several important issues in Shandong Province.

1. Banditry: Banditry in Shandong Province did not begin today, but it is especially rampant after the war. The most famous areas are Jiaodong and western and southwestern Shandong. These bandits appear and disappear unpredictably, and they have been formally recognized and used by each other, so their equipment is also very sufficient. The official soldiers' capabilities are not worth mentioning, and the responsibility of suppressing them is not easy. Sometimes, they act as local militias and sometimes win the hearts of the people to resist the government troops, so a fundamental solution is impossible. For example, the troops under Xue Chuanfeng in the southwestern Yangu area have been formally appointed by the Jin side as the commander of the Special Operations Brigade. He is a native of southwestern Shandong and is very familiar with the local situation. In fact, it is very difficult for government troops to open up the area. It is quite difficult to eradicate them due to the lack of troops, and the mobilization of guest troops is also quite difficult. For example, although Liu Zhennian's troops in Jiaodong only have 30,000 soldiers, their combat effectiveness is very high after Liu's strict training. However, it is virtually impossible to obtain Liu's full responsibility for suppressing banditry. As a result, Han's troops suddenly go east and suddenly go west, and the banditry is never defeated. As a result, although Shandong Province has been pacified, banditry is no less weak than military disasters. As for the losses suffered by the people due to banditry, the official authorities have not investigated or assumed responsibility. However, the provincial government must receive reports of bandit alerts every day, which is a fact.

2. Finance: According to the new budget for Shandong Province in the 19th year, the total annual revenue is 28,887,057 yuan, and the expenditure, according to the published figures, is also the same amount. However, the land tax item in the revenue is 14,847,209 yuan, which is the amount determined previously. Now, this land tax has long been pre-collected by the previous warlords. If the provincial government still needs to maintain this amount, it must emulate the previous successor's preparation. I would like to ask if the people, in the state of being covered in wounds and eyes, have the ability to bear this burden. Moreover, if the various regular and miscellaneous taxes and levies total no less than 2.6 million yuan per year, these taxes and levies mostly involve harsh details. If wise governance begins, the number of annual expenditures maintained in its original state is bound to lose half of its numbers. At present, the area of ​​Shandong Province can actually be divided into three parts: one is the area under Han Fuqu's command in Jinan and central and northern Shandong, one is the area under Liu Zhennian's command in Jiaodong, and one is the area under Ma Hongkui's command in southern Shandong. The systems of these parts of the army are not related to each other, and all administrative matters are managed separately. The tax collection agencies do not need to be mentioned, so the total amount of income mentioned above still needs to be reduced by two parts. It is obvious that the income is not enough to cover the expenditure, and there is no way to deal with the financial situation. The plan to rectify the provincial government has become a pie in the sky.

3. Aggression: Shandong Province has suffered no less oppression from the Japanese than the two provinces of Jilin and Liaoning, and the most fearful thing is economic aggression. The arrangements in Qingdao are indisputable. In Jinan, the crisis and heartbreaking places are even more numerous. Here are two examples: one is poison. Since Han Fuqu took office as chairman of Shandong Province, he has been strictly enforcing the ban on smoking. It is said that anyone who violates the ban will be shot upon discovery. A 13-year-old child who was found with opium paste was subjected to extreme punishment. It can be seen that the authorities are determined to ban drugs, but the authorities can only prohibit Chinese people from trafficking and smoking privately, but cannot stop the Japanese from selling them. As a result, those who are prohibited from selling privately are only increasing the Japanese's private pockets, and the victims of the Chinese have become even more serious. The second is that according to investigations by Japanese pawnshops, there are more than 50 Japanese-run pawnshops in Shandong Province, taking Jinan as an example. The reason for their development is that, passively, the Chinese government cannot protect Chinese pawnshops and allows soldiers to harass them, which ultimately leads to their closure, leaving the Japanese to rise up and take their place. Actively, the Japanese operate this industry without relying on our country's laws and doing whatever they want. The profits are generous and there is no competition from Chinese people, so their business is booming, and the people of the five countries are subjected to the most vicious exploitation. The usual practice of Japanese pawnshops is that the interest rate is 10%, and they cannot be redeemed after three months, and the pawn price is extremely low, often less than one-tenth of the original price. For example, those who pawn at the end of the month will be charged for two months by Japanese merchants on the first day of the following month, even though it is clearly a two-day period. All disputes are noted on the pawn ticket in accordance with Japanese law, so in the event of litigation, the fault always lies with the pawner. The villagers can only endure the pain of pawning with cash, which is no different from drinking poison to quench their thirst. What has been said above is still a very small matter. If the government can pay attention to the suffering of the people, it is still not impossible to recover. The most fearful thing is that the Japanese have concrete and large-scale economic aggression plans. The details cannot be accommodated in this article and will be reported in another article after investigation.

4. Party Affairs: The party affairs in Shandong Province are completely isolated from the people. The situation is no different from that in the provinces of Pingjin and Hebei, and its intervention in local judicial administration is excessive. We do not need to specify when this phenomenon began, but it is a fact that Shandong Province has had this weakness in the past. According to reports, there are only three to four thousand registered and qualified party members in Shandong Province, which is less than one-thousandth of the total population of the province. Although the residents are simple and robust, they can still obey orders. If the senior party leaders are well-led, party affairs in Shandong Province are easiest to carry out and will also be a major aid to the party. Unfortunately, those who have handled party affairs in the past have always regarded themselves as another class, and their arrogance has been overwhelming, and their private morals have often not been self-examined, resulting in the loss of the people's faith. The political enemies of the central government often use this to attack Jiang himself or the entire government, but in reality, they are all caused by the party's bad image. Although the current rectification committee has an insufficient number of people, the person in charge still knows to first send inspectors to various places to conduct a thorough investigation of the status of party affairs in preparation for future rectification. The reporter hopes to establish a solid connection with the people in the midst of changing the course and seeking change. The above is only a summary of the four major aspects. Other measures such as the urgent need to rectify river affairs, the effective elimination of miscellaneous troops, the reduction of military quotas, the abolition of miscellaneous taxes and levies, and the cessation of pre-collection of land taxes are all essential measures to save Shandong. The authorities should reflect on this, and the people of Shandong should rise up and urge the government to implement them.

Social News Submission Guidelines 219

(1) The text should be related to domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, and rural areas.

(2) News on hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life is limited to illustrations. Various lyrical paintings related to social life are preferred.

(3) Photographs of seasonal events, landscapes, flora and fauna, people, and news photography are qualified. Photographs of beautiful women in seasonal and landscape photography are especially welcome.

(4) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally. The writing should not be sloppy. Western text should be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black drawings.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript should be sent to the Social News Editorial Department.

(9) All manuscripts, whether published or not, will not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The remuneration for illustrations and photos is the same per piece. Special manuscripts will be remunerated separately.

Theater News 220

The Odeon Company announced that among the sound films produced by the American First National Film Company this year, there are two sister films: Paris and Lillies of the Field. These two films are not only great productions of the First National Film Company, but also the most honorable works on the American silver screen this year. Paris is the crystallization of the French famous singer and dancer Irene Bordoni's first appearance on the screen. Lillies of the Field is the last masterpiece of the orchid girl Colleen Moore. Ms. Irene is famous for her singing and dancing and is one of the three famous singers and dancers in the world. Some film companies in the United States admired her and offered her a large sum of money to star in the film. At that time, sound films had not yet been invented, but Ms. Irene declined, believing that although the art of dance could be enhanced by film, the beauty of song could not be expressed by silver light. After sound films were invented, the First National Film Company sincerely invited her to star in Paris. The film was shown in a large theater in New York. At the same time, Paramount Company's The Godless Girl was also released. As a result, the audience sighed that it was impossible to have both bear's paw and fish. As a result, both films sold out every day, and the ticket price increased from 2 US dollars to 6 US dollars. It was necessary to purchase them two weeks in advance to get a seat. It can be imagined that they were a sensation at the time and were welcomed by the audience. The Godless Girl has been shown in Shanghai several times, while Paris only arrived in Shanghai last week. It is now scheduled to be shown at the most luxurious and magnificent new Cathay Theater in Shanghai, which is about to open. As for its sister film Lillies of the Field, it has not yet arrived in Shanghai.

Women's Life

The Story of the Vest 224

— Wen Juan

The fallen leaves of the plane trees flutter and fall onto the grass. A dozen or so benches stand quietly, waiting for their masters to arrive.

After the four o'clock dismissal bell, the female students rush into the campus, each holding various kinds of yarn and vests and clothes that they have just started working on or that are already half-finished.

They find their seats and sit down one after another. Those who can't get a bench squeeze in with others, sometimes three people sharing one bench. The clamor and laughter begin.

("Your vest is really nice. The bean paste color matches the trim. Oh, the buttons are sewn on too, also bean paste color. No wonder I couldn't find you after school yesterday. You were matching buttons. Mr. A is really lucky!") Before Ping finishes speaking, someone pinches her leg. She cries out softly ("Ouch!").

A leaf falls on Ping's hair, and a green caterpillar crawls out from under the leaf. Wen, who is sitting next to her, screams. Everyone, not knowing why, leaves their seats to watch.

("What's so scary about this?") Ying, nicknamed "Wild Zhang Fei," reaches out to grab it and even shows off her skills by deliberately letting the worm crawl on her nose.

Wen has already jumped into the middle of the ground and hides her face in her hands.

Those students who were "squatting by the edge of the benches" take the opportunity to occupy other people's spots.

By the time they finish dealing with the "worm case" and return to their original positions, they see those who replaced them smiling proudly.

Seeing that this carousel-like game is too tiring, they propose sitting on the ground. Suddenly, handkerchiefs flutter like butterflies, and a dozen people sit in a circle and start singing.

The singing and the small, crisp sound of knitting needles combine to create a wonderful music. The environment of V University is originally quiet, and the campus is far from the sports field. At this time, all is silent, and the singing reaches the autumn sky. The clear white clouds also crane their necks to listen quietly. The plane trees sway their branches, making a rustling sound that echoes the people's singing.

("You're really having fun!") A dozen or so mouths on the chairs say at the same time, inviting them to join the circle. Their group immediately gets larger and becomes oval-shaped.

Black Vest – New Autumn Outfit 225

— Bing She

The singing stops for a moment, and the vest debate is declared revived.

("Life is important! People aren't waiting to wear it, so don't rush like this. Take a break before continuing.")

("What do you mean, people aren't waiting? It's for my mother.")

("Haha, the old lady is wearing a green western vest! This is Miss Qin's new fashion invention. Come quickly, everyone, and take a look!") Wild Zhang Fei sings loudly in the style of a shop clerk calling for customers.

Qin's face turns red, and she lowers her head in silence.

"Aren't you going to hit her? This big guy is getting more and more naughty," Qin's neighbor encourages.

Thin-faced Qin and Wild Zhang Fei wrestle into a ball. With a clatter, a knitting needle breaks, and people from both sides come out to pull them apart. The power struggle turns into a verbal battle. Those who joined the battle group want to show off their eloquence and temporarily put down the work in their hands.

("Does knitting a vest necessarily mean it's for a lover? Can't people have older brothers and younger brothers at home who can wear vests?")

("Of course, older brothers and younger brothers can wear them, but this vest will tell me that it's for someone special. I can't lie for the vest.")

("Don't argue. There will be evidence when it's worn.")

("That's right!") A few people agree.

Most people lower their heads and awkwardly pull at the grass.

The red hibiscus flowers by the wall pile up like clouds, which is truly beautiful. The setting sun shines faintly on the branches of the deciduous trees, as if saying good night to people, indicating that it is about to return. Small birds chirp, and a gust of west wind swirls the fallen leaves in the air. The innocent laughter of the girls adds some joy to this twilight hour.

("There's a French test tomorrow! I don't know if you've been reviewing. You've been too busy making trouble. What are you going to do?") The voice of someone resembling a teacher startles everyone. Looking closely, Wild Zhang Fei stands straight, making everyone else bend over with laughter.

("Don't pay attention to her. French is just old T's thing anyway. It doesn't matter.")

("But we should still go look at the books.") Ping, sitting under the tree, says this and stands up at the same time, brushing off the dirt. She grumbles, "I only finished one inch today. It's getting cold. When will I ever finish this? It's so annoying being with you little sparrows." She pretends to be angry.

("You were the one who led the trouble just now, and now you're complaining about others. You're really shameless.")

They both laugh. The circular formation has already dispersed. Everyone stands up one after another. Those who are anxious about tomorrow's exam leave first. The most mischievous ones make trouble for a while longer before slowly walking with gliding steps toward the self-study room.

The air on campus suddenly becomes calm. Only these mute benches will forever keep the secret of their conversation.

Women's Life Submission Guidelines 226

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of women's issues, domestic and international news about women, descriptions of women's lives, essays, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Illustrations should be related to women's issues.

(3) Photographs related to women's news, women's issues, and women's lives are welcome, whether individual or group photos.

The maximum length of each article should not exceed two thousand words.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(5) The maximum length of each article should not exceed two thousand words.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally. Do not be sloppy with the writing. Avoid using Western text if possible. If it is absolutely necessary to cite the original text, it must be attached below the text.

Youth Corner

Impressions of a Trip North 227

— Su Ling

(20) At the Chinese Eastern Railway Club

Early in the morning, Ou and Miss Zhu came to find me. I was still asleep. I groggily got up, thinking that they must be going somewhere to play again. However, Ou is about to take his graduation exam, so it doesn't seem like he'll have time to play.

("Oh, you're not up yet? Hurry, hurry... get up, get up! Miss Zhu is waiting outside. Her skin will suffer in the sun.")

("Okay, I'll be quick. Please invite Miss Zhu inside.")

("No, just hurry up and wash, and come out immediately.")

I forgot to ask him what was going on and hurriedly threw on my clothes. I didn't even tie my tie before Ou pulled me out.

("This is Miss Zhu. This is Mister Su—Su, come, come, let's go to the coffee shop in front to have an ice before we go.")

("What's going on? Why are you so busy? Aren't you supposed to be taking the exam?")

("The exam? It's really funny. Miss Zhu and I went to Professor X's house early this morning to take it because we had a makeup exam today.")

We sat at a table in the coffee shop and ordered three ices, which stopped Ou's and Miss Zhu's sweating.

("After we eat, let's go find Ningqiu to ask him for tickets to the Fada Drama. I originally thought that Old Xie would have them, but he didn't. I think Ningqiu will definitely have them. Do you know where he lives?")

("He's still with Changhong.")

We finished our ices and then took the streetcar to find Ningqiu.

Unfortunately, Ningqiu had already gone to Fada, leaving Changhong alone in the room smoking. We had no choice but to split up.

……………

In the evening, Ou came again.

("I got the tickets. Let's go. It's at the Chinese Eastern Railway Club. I don't think you've been there before. You should go. There's a large theater inside, and there are also many books.")

This play was originally for disaster relief. It's really inappropriate for us to go see it for free. However, we poor people really can't do anything about disaster relief.

("We're only going to see the play directed by Ningqiu.")

("What play is Ningqiu directing?")

("Father Returns. Ningqiu told me yesterday that it's going well.")

………………………

We arrived at the Chinese Eastern Railway Club. The building of this club is naturally the only one in Harbin. The walls of the theater are decorated with delicate bas-reliefs. There is a delicate lamp in the center of the theater, and everything on the stage is very complete, with very realistic sets, and the lighting changes are also well-equipped.

The curtain opened. At first, these plays were really bad. Sometimes, you would see many performances that made you nauseous. Then Ou led me to the living room to look at books.

There were several reproductions of famous paintings. The technique was very skillful. One of the larger ones was a painting of a Cossack story. Several other landscapes seemed to be copied from the works of an English painter. The painting method was very detailed, but under the light and hung too high, I couldn't see them closely.

We rested on the sofa for a while and then went back to our seats. Then "Father Returns" started.

Before the performance, someone informed the audience of some viewing rules, because in the previous few plays, the audience was chaotically clamoring. This made the audience feel that "Father Returns" might be a very serious play, so after the curtain opened, the audience was silent.

Ningqiu didn't use the original realistic sets in the theater. He only used a few pieces of black cloth to simply line the back. Because of the lighting, it didn't seem inappropriate.

The spirit of the whole play lies in your own appearance on stage. When you, the wandering father, said ("When people get old, they think of home... Alas, I always want to earn a thousand or two thousand yuan to bring home... But fate is teasing me, and even the little house in the circus is burned down"),

and when Xian Yilang angrily shouted at his father ("Father, I've never had a father like you who loved me. I created everything myself... You suddenly broke into someone else's house and want people to call you father..."), some of the audience were actually shedding tears. After the play was over, Ou sighed and said to me:

("I'm afraid Ningqiu himself will become like this father in the future.")

But I myself am terrified that I might become this father.

Holiday – Ye Garden – Wusong 228

— Guangmei

Although college students have reached the stage where they should be autonomous, there are many ways in which they are no more advanced than elementary school students. Elementary school students like it when the teacher takes a day off and the school is closed. College students are no different. It seems that I still remember when I was studying in a private school as a child, I often dreamed that the teacher wouldn't come for three out of five days. I simply hoped that our school would face west. Whenever I saw the sun about to cross the stone steps of the study room, we would spontaneously discuss with each other ("The teacher may not come today. The sun is about to reach the doorstep. I didn't see the teacher mention it yesterday either.") ("Maybe he's sick.") ("That's right. I don't want the teacher to die, I don't want the teacher to be dead, I just want the teacher to be sleeping in bed.") Under these circumstances, although we spoke energetically, our hearts were pounding with anxiety, fearing that the teacher would suddenly come in. It was really very childish at that time. We were all young children under the age of ten, so whenever we really had a holiday or the teacher announced ("I won't be here tomorrow."), especially when the teacher didn't give advance notice and didn't come midway, this feeling was the most intense. It was as if birds in a cage had been released and scattered with a bang. Also, every time it was near the Dragon Boat Festival or the Mid-Autumn Festival, and even more so for the New Year, we would spend at least half a month counting down the days. After the holidays were over, we would worry about having to go back to school. At this time, my grandfather and

Page 26

My uncles and fathers would often tease people by saying ("Hey, you have to put on the bridle again. Hurry up and study hard, or you'll get beaten by the teacher.") This scene is as if it happened yesterday. However, looking back, how can one bear it? Alas, where has my childhood innocence disappeared to? Now, I am a college student and should no longer be like before, only willing to study under the strict authority of the teacher. However, bad habits are hard to break. After all, I still like it when the school is closed. There is no way around it.

Yesterday was the school's anniversary. In the morning, we only held a very simple ceremony. In the afternoon, we planned how to spend this holiday. First, Zhen and Xia proposed ("Let's go to Ye Garden in Jiangwan.") ("Second..."). ("I agree..."). So all five of us in the room agreed. We had been coveting Ye Garden for a long time, and now we finally had such an opportunity. While Yu went to get tickets for us, everyone brushed their shoes, slicked their hair, and lightly applied a layer of makeup, except for Xia. ("Everyone, don't wear high-heeled shoes. Wait a minute, you'll suffer and regret it.") ("Who's trying to look good like that? It's not like we're going out as guests.") ("Really, who are you dressing up for?") Everyone took care of each other, saying one thing or another. Although I didn't pay attention, I had it in mind. So I took a piece of white paper, wrapped my white cloth sneakers, and lightly tucked them under my arm in case I needed them.

("How quiet and secluded this is. It's simply a paradise on earth.") As soon as we entered the garden, everyone said these two general sentences in unison. Fortunately, Zhen had been here before, so we chose her as our guide. Wherever we went, we lingered, reluctant to leave. Seeing the clever artificial rocks and the places where we could take photos, I was always extremely annoyed that I hadn't asked someone to come with us to take pictures. However, in a helpless moment, I would comfort myself by saying ("Alas, who could have known there would be such wonderful scenery?")

The garden's novel layout, unique construction, and well-equipped facilities, especially the cleverness of the artificial rocks, are beyond my clumsy pen to describe fully. To tell the truth, foolish me, although I wandered for a long time, still couldn't get a bird's-eye view of it. Ye also said to me ("It's really impossible to write a travelogue. It's too good, the scope is too wide, and every place and every scene is good. How can you bear to part with any of it? Oh, it's too beautiful to take in and too much to remember.")

The garden's special feature is that it seems to be built in the mountains. The elevations rise and fall, no different from Loxia Mountain. The construction of the artificial rocks, with winding paths leading to secluded places, with small holes to enter and exit, is similar to the Twelve Caves of Yan Mountain ("The mountain has a small mouth, as if there is light..."), which coincides unexpectedly. When encountering such a situation, Xia and I always argue about who gets to say ("I want to be a gardener here.") ("After I turn forty and have fulfilled my responsibilities to the country and society, I will definitely come here and discuss with the garden owner about letting me be a gardener here.") We even want to turn into a fish, a bird, even a fly is happy. Although this is inevitably too much like sitting in a well and looking at the sky, being in this sea of ten feet of soft red all the time, it's no wonder we have this kind of greed.

In the depths of a bamboo forest is surrounded a Chinese-style house carved full of gold patterns. The terrain of the house is very low, but it is cleverly recessed in the bamboo forest, so we search for the entrance to the house.

We ascend to that secluded place in the bamboo forest, reluctant to leave it. At the same time, everyone cries out unexpectedly ("Oh, why don't I feel happy in my heart? Instead, I feel sad and just want to cry, but I can't cry for any particular reason. What's the matter? Could it be that happiness to the extreme will make you want to cry?") It's really too difficult to make people feel bad. Whenever we encounter better scenery, we initially shout like crazy, but immediately the feeling in our hearts turns into a sour taste. This kind of sourness caused by happiness is definitely different from what the romantics call melancholy. We simply don't know whether to laugh or cry, and an unknown mixed reaction rises in our hearts. Our mouths also express the same contradictory feelings ("Oh, how poetic, but I just want to cry.") ("Isn't that right? Who doesn't want to cry?") Everyone has this common psychology.

Although the scenery is good, it's not a place to stay for long. We reluctantly harden our hearts and say goodbye to Ye Garden. I'm afraid that even when parting with a lover, we wouldn't be so reluctant as we are now.

It was still early, about half past three. There were no cars when we left, so we walked to the racecourse. Xia proposed that we continue to Wusong. I seconded the proposal, followed by Ye, Cheng, and Zhen. The two of them cried that they were dizzy and their feet hurt, so they took a bus back to school. Xia, Ye, and I took a car to Jiangwan and then took a train. Then I went to Tongji to call Mao. The two of them went to Zhonggong first to look for Old Xuejin and Ms. Meng, and agreed to meet at Zhonggong half an hour later to go to Paotai Bay. Fortunately, we all met, but Miss Jin was uncomfortable and went back to Shanghai, which was regrettable.

Oh, the students nearby are really comfortable. After class and after dinner, they can come to the riverside to stroll at any time. On a moonlit night like today, there is an unspeakable joy, mystery, and taste. It is truly a place for uncivilized people. In the summer evenings, it's nice to come and cool off, and if you're happy, you can play musical instruments such as the flute, clarinet, and violin. It's so great that it's indescribable. It has the atmosphere of a poet's life. At the same time, the rushing waters of the Huangpu River can very much arouse people's upward will, broaden their minds, and even evoke people's revolutionary emotions, bravery, and action. It can also break down the concept of individualism. In that great natural realm, you can feel that the individual is particularly small.

The moon goddess accompanied us so enthusiastically that we were happy and forgot to return.

We were honored by Meng and the others' warm hospitality. They insisted on inviting us to a late dinner. We couldn't refuse their kindness. However, we never expected Meng to be so polite. Even now, when I think about it, I still feel uneasy. We also made noise for a long time, preventing them from studying. I feel even more sorry.

The train seemed to be deliberately making things difficult for us. We waited for a full quarter of an hour. By the time we got to Tiantong'an, it was already half past ten. At this time, the quiet Jiangwan Road was only occupied by the three of us, who were happy to say a witty remark ("Jiangwan Road is for the three of us.") The moonlight shone on the asphalt road, shining brightly. Clearly, the moon goddess was welcoming and protecting us.

Youth Corner Submission Guidelines 229

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of youth issues, domestic and international school or student news, descriptions of school life, essays, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Illustrations should be related to youth issues.

(3) Photographs related to youth life (such as sports, travel, excursions, plays, speeches, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), new school openings, and youth movements are welcome, whether individual or group photos.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the paper.
